N. et al. Nuclear accumulation of CHMP7 initiates nuclear pore complex injury and subsequent TDP-43 dysfunction in sporadic and familial ALS. Sci. Transl. Med. 13, eabe1923 (2021)."). Notably, decreasing levels of CHMP7 or CHMP2B via antisense oligonucleotides (ASOs) was sufficient to repair nuclear pore complex integrity and TDP-43 function in an induced pluripotent stem cell model of sALS and *C9orf72*-associated ALS/FTD[64](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR64 "Coyne, A. N. et al. Nuclear accumulation of CHMP7 initiates nuclear pore complex injury and subsequent TDP-43 dysfunction in sporadic and familial ALS. Sci. Transl. Med. 13, eabe1923 (2021)."),[145](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR145 "Keeley, O., Mendoza, E., Menon, D. & Coyne, A. N. CHMP2B promotes CHMP7 mediated nuclear pore complex injury in sporadic ALS. Acta Neuropathol. Commun. 12, 199 (2024)."), highlighting the therapeutic potential of targeting ESCRT proteins in neurodegeneration. Supporting these in vitro studies, knockdown of multiple ESCRT-III proteins by RNA-mediated interference was neuroprotective in a *Drosophila* model of *C9orf72*-associated disease[146](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR146 "Dubey, S. K., Maulding, K., Sung, H. & Lloyd, T. E. Nucleoporins are degraded via upregulation of ESCRT-III/Vps4 complex in Drosophila models of C9-ALS/FTD. Cell Rep. 40, 111379 (2022).").

Alterations in nuclear membrane architecture are prevalent in neurodegenerative diseases including *C9orf72*-associated ALS/FTD and tauopathies[147](#ref-CR147 "Frost, B., Bardai, F. H. & Feany, M. B. Lamin dysfunction mediates neurodegeneration in tauopathies. Curr. Biol. 26, 129–136 (2016)."),[148](#ref-CR148 "Eftekharzadeh, B. et al. Tau protein disrupts nucleocytoplasmic transport in Alzheimer’s disease. Neuron 99, 925–940.e927 (2018)."),[149](#ref-CR149 "Paonessa, F. et al. Microtubules deform the nuclear membrane and disrupt nucleocytoplasmic transport in tau-mediated frontotemporal dementia. Cell Rep. 26, 582–593.e585 (2019)."),[150](#ref-CR150 "Sirtori, R. et al. LINC complex alterations are a key feature of sporadic and familial ALS/FTD. Acta Neuropathol. Commun. 12, 69 (2024)."),[151](#ref-CR151 "Sirtori, R. et al. Altered nuclear envelope homeostasis is a key pathogenic event in C9ORF72-linked ALS/FTD. Preprint at bioRxiv
https://doi.org/10.1101/2024.02.01.578318
(2024)."),[152](#ref-CR152 "Giampetruzzi, A. et al. Modulation of actin polymerization affects nucleocytoplasmic transport in multiple forms of amyotrophic lateral sclerosis. Nat. Commun. 10, 3827 (2019)."),[153](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR153 "Ortega, J. A. et al. Nucleocytoplasmic proteomic analysis uncovers eRF1 and nonsense-mediated decay as modifiers of ALS/FTD C9orf72 toxicity. Neuron 106, 90–107.e113 (2020)."). However, the contribution of ESCRT alterations to this pathology remains controversial. For instance, one study using a tauopathy model suggests that overexpression of specific ESCRT proteins is neuroprotective[154](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR154 "Prissette, M. et al. Disruption of nuclear envelope integrity as a possible initiating event in tauopathies. Cell Rep. 40, 111249 (2022). This study examines the potential for therapeutically modulating ESCRT expression to mitigate nuclear envelope alterations in tauopathy."), whereas a study using a *C9orf72*-associated ALS model found that a reduction of ESCRT protein dwell time at the nuclear envelope was protective[150](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR150 "Sirtori, R. et al. LINC complex alterations are a key feature of sporadic and familial ALS/FTD. Acta Neuropathol. Commun. 12, 69 (2024)."). CHMP2B is recruited to sites of membrane damage after sealing to facilitate removal of damaged membranes from the cell, a process that is disrupted by mutations in CHMP2B[143](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR143 "Heffner, C. M., Starling, G. P., Isaacs, A. M. & Carlton, J. G. The ALS- and FTD-associated proteins annexin A11 and CHMP2B act sequentially in membrane repair. Preprint at bioRxiv
https://doi.org/10.1101/2024.11.19.624330
(2024)."). New evidence suggests a homeostatic, rather than solely injury-responsive, mechanism for ESCRTs[70](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR70 "Chen, W., Motsinger, M. M., Li, J., Bohannon, K. P. & Hanson, P. I. Ca2+-sensor ALG-2 engages ESCRTs to enhance lysosomal membrane resilience to osmotic stress. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 121, e2318412121 (2024)."), although this remains to be confirmed across a broader range of physiological cell types.

A defining feature of neurodegenerative diseases is the accumulation of protein aggregates[155](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR155 "Wu, J., Wu, J., Chen, T., Cai, J. & Ren, R. Protein aggregation and its affecting mechanisms in neurodegenerative diseases. Neurochem. Int. 180, 105880 (2024)."). In Alzheimer’s disease and Parkinson’s disease, these pathologic protein aggregates are thought to be propagated to neighbouring cells in a prion-like manner[156](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR156 "Jucker, M. & Walker, L. C. Self-propagation of pathogenic protein aggregates in neurodegenerative diseases. Nature 501, 45–51 (2013)."), thereby ‘spreading’ disease throughout the central nervous system[157](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR157 "Uemura, N., Uemura, M. T., Luk, K. C., Lee, V. M. & Trojanowski, J. Q. Cell-to-cell transmission of tau and α-synuclein. Trends Mol. Med. 26, 936–952 (2020)."). Extracellular vesicle release is thought to be one pathway by which protein aggregates can spread between cells in neurodegeneration[158](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR158 "Peng, C., Trojanowski, J. Q. & Lee, V. M. Protein transmission in neurodegenerative disease. Nat. Rev. Neurol. 16, 199–212 (2020)."). Recent work has demonstrated that impaired ESCRT function promotes the propagation of tau fibrils[159](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR159 "Rose, K. et al. Tau fibrils induce nanoscale membrane damage and nucleate cytosolic tau at lysosomes. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 121, e2315690121 (2024)."). Specifically, the ESCRT-III protein CHMP6 has been found to act as a suppressor of tau escape[160](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR160 "Chen, J. J. et al. Compromised function of the ESCRT pathway promotes endolysosomal escape of tau seeds and propagation of tau aggregation. J. Biol. Chem. 294, 18952–18966 (2019)."). In addition to the role of ESCRTs in endolysosomal turnover of aggregation-prone proteins[161](#ref-CR161 "Filimonenko, M. et al. Functional multivesicular bodies are required for autophagic clearance of protein aggregates associated with neurodegenerative disease. J. Cell Biol. 179, 485–500 (2007)."),[162](#ref-CR162 "Liu, G. et al. Endocytosis regulates TDP-43 toxicity and turnover. Nat. Commun. 8, 2092 (2017)."),[163](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR163 "Borland, H. et al. α-Synuclein buildup is alleviated via ESCRT-dependent endosomal degradation brought about by p38MAPK inhibition in cells expressing p25α. J. Biol. Chem. 298, 102531 (2022)."), in neurons and astrocytes treated with tau preformed fibrils, ESCRTs are recruited to lysosomes where they serve to mitigate lysosome damage[159](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR159 "Rose, K. et al. Tau fibrils induce nanoscale membrane damage and nucleate cytosolic tau at lysosomes. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 121, e2315690121 (2024)."). ESCRT–ubiquitin inclusions are observed to increase in transdifferentiated neurons (tNeurons) derived from patients with Alzheimer’s disease[164](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR164 "Chou, C. C. et al. Human tNeurons reveal aging-linked proteostasis deficits driving Alzheimer’s phenotypes. Res. Sq.
https://doi.org/10.21203/rs.3.rs-4407236/v1
(2024)."). The ability of exogenous tau preformed fibrils to damage lysosomes and spread in a receiver cell is increased by expression of mutant CHMP2B[159](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR159 "Rose, K. et al. Tau fibrils induce nanoscale membrane damage and nucleate cytosolic tau at lysosomes. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 121, e2315690121 (2024)."). In Parkinson’s disease, α-synuclein accumulation is mediated, at least in part, by alterations in endolysosomal function, and disrupting interactions between α-synuclein and ESCRT proteins is protective in models of Parkinson’s disease[163](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR163 "Borland, H. et al. α-Synuclein buildup is alleviated via ESCRT-dependent endosomal degradation brought about by p38MAPK inhibition in cells expressing p25α. J. Biol. Chem. 298, 102531 (2022)."),[165](#ref-CR165 "Nim, S. et al. Disrupting the α-synuclein-ESCRT interaction with a peptide inhibitor mitigates neurodegeneration in preclinical models of Parkinson’s disease. Nat. Commun. 14, 2150 (2023)."),[166](#ref-CR166 "Spencer, B. et al. α-Synuclein interferes with the ESCRT-III complex contributing to the pathogenesis of Lewy body disease. Hum. Mol. Genet. 25, 1100–1115 (2016). References 166,167 examine modulation of ESCRT–α-synuclein interactions to alleviate neurodegeneration in Parkinson’s disease."),[167](#ref-CR167 "Zenko, D. et al. Monitoring α-synuclein ubiquitination dynamics reveals key endosomal effectors mediating its trafficking and degradation. Sci. Adv. 9, eadd8910 (2023)."),[168](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR168 "Sitron, C. S. et al. α-Synuclein aggregates inhibit ESCRT-III through sequestration and collateral degradation. Preprint at bioRxiv
https://doi.org/10.1101/2025.01.13.632710
(2025).").

### ESCRT proteins in neurodevelopmental disorders

ESCRT protein mutations and dysfunction have also been linked to disruptions in neurodevelopment (Table [1](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#Tab1)). Autosomal recessive mutations in PTPN23 cause microcephaly, developmental delay and epilepsy[169](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR169 "Sowada, N. et al. Mutations of PTPN23 in developmental and epileptic encephalopathy. Hum. Genet. 136, 1455–1461 (2017)."). Autosomal dominant mutations that result in truncation of UBAP1 protein cause hereditary spastic paraplegia[170](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR170 "Farazi Fard, M. A. et al. Truncating mutations in UBAP1 cause hereditary spastic paraplegia. Am. J. Hum. Genet. 104, 767–773 (2019).") and variants in SNF8 (also known as EAP30 or VPS22) can cause a range of neurological abnormalities, including neurodevelopmental arrest, intellectual disability and ataxia[171](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR171 "Brugger, M. et al. Bi-allelic variants in SNF8 cause a disease spectrum ranging from severe developmental and epileptic encephalopathy to syndromic optic atrophy. Am. J. Hum. Genet. 111, 594–613 (2024)."). Missense mutations in the ATPase domain of VPS4A can cause multisystem disease characterized by delayed neurodevelopment, altered growth and anaemia[172](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR172 "Rodger, C. et al. De novo VPS4A mutations cause multisystem disease with abnormal neurodevelopment. Am. J. Hum. Genet. 107, 1129–1148 (2020)."),[173](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR173 "Seu, K. G. et al. VPS4A mutations in humans cause syndromic congenital dyserythropoietic anemia due to cytokinesis and trafficking defects. Am. J. Hum. Genet. 107, 1149–1156 (2020)."). Additionally, autosomal recessive loss-of-function mutations in CHMP1A have been associated with microcephaly and pontocerebellar hypoplasia[174](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR174 "Mochida, G. H. et al. CHMP1A encodes an essential regulator of BMI1–INK4A in cerebellar development. Nat. Genet. 44, 1260–1264 (2012)."). Mechanistically, CHMP1A knockout in mice led to impairments in ILV formation and decreased extracellular vesicle-dependent secretion of critical neurodevelopmental factors, including sonic hedgehog[175](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR175 "Coulter, M. E. et al. The ESCRT-III protein CHMP1A mediates secretion of sonic hedgehog on a distinctive subtype of extracellular vesicles. Cell Rep. 24, 973–986.e978 (2018)."). A homozygous variant of CHMP3 is associated with complex hereditary spastic paraplegia, possibly due to aberrant autophagy[176](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR176 "Cohen-Barak, E. et al. A homozygous variant in CHMP3 is associated with complex hereditary spastic paraplegia. J. Med. Genet. 60, 233–240 (2023)."). Although not known to be a genetic cause of neurodevelopmental disorders, disruptions in the function of CHMP4B have been linked to alterations in synaptic maturation, maintenance and function[177](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR177 "Vita, D. J. & Broadie, K. ESCRT-III membrane trafficking misregulation contributes to fragile X syndrome synaptic defects. Sci. Rep. 7, 8683 (2017)."),[178](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR178 "Sears, J. C. & Broadie, K. Fragile X mental retardation protein regulates activity-dependent membrane trafficking and trans-synaptic signaling mediating synaptic remodeling. Front. Mol. Neurosci. 10, 440 (2017)."). Moreover, loss of ESCRT-I and ESCRT-III proteins in the *Drosophila* peripheral nervous system results in a reduction in the size of the dendritic field with a concomitant increase in dendritic branching[179](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR179 "Sweeney, N. T., Brenman, J. E., Jan, Y. N. & Gao, F. B. The coiled-coil protein shrub controls neuronal morphogenesis in Drosophila. Curr. Biol. 16, 1006–1011 (2006)."),[180](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR180 "Loncle, N., Agromayor, M., Martin-Serrano, J. & Williams, D. W. An ESCRT module is required for neuron pruning. Sci. Rep. 5, 8461 (2015)."), indicating a role for ESCRTs in neuronal pruning. Overall, most of the pathologies associated with ESCRT dysfunctions in neurons are related to their functions in endosomal sorting and biogenesis of MVEs and exosomes, but other functions such as lysosome repair are also likely to be involved.

## Conclusions and perspectives

The explosion of new information about the functions of ESCRT proteins in disease raises the question of whether ESCRTs might be suitable targets for therapies. In general, ESCRTs are dependency factors for viruses, including HIV-1. RetroCHMP3, a dominant-negative ESCRT-III variant that occurs naturally in New World monkeys and mice, acts as in host defence by interfering with the scission step in retroviral release[181](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR181 "Rheinemann, L. et al. RetroCHMP3 blocks budding of enveloped viruses without blocking cytokinesis. Cell 184, 5419–5431.e5416 (2021)."), with little effect on endogenous cell functions. This provides proof of principle for selective inhibition of ESCRTs to prevent viral release without affecting other cellular functions. Tantalosin, a small-molecule inhibitor of the ESCRT-III protein IST1[182](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR182 "Knyazeva, A. et al. A chemical inhibitor of IST1–CHMP1B interaction impairs endosomal recycling and induces noncanonical LC3 lipidation. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 121, e2317680121 (2024)."), breaks up protein–protein interactions in the ESCRT-III lattice, demonstrating that protein–protein interactions in this system are targetable. VPS4A and VPS4B are the only enzymes in the ESCRT system, however their essential role in normal cell functions suggests that a pan-specific VPS4 inhibitor would be toxic. The synthetic lethality between VPS4A and VPS4B[122](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR122 "Szymanska, E. et al. Synthetic lethality between VPS4A and VPS4B triggers an inflammatory response in colorectal cancer. EMBO Mol. Med. 12, e10812 (2020)."),[123](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR123 "Neggers, J. E. et al. Synthetic lethal interaction between the ESCRT paralog enzymes VPS4A and VPS4B in cancers harboring loss of chromosome 18q or 16q. Cell Rep. 33, 108493 (2020). References 122,123 uncover the molecular basis of synthetic lethality between VPS4A and VPS4B, and its possible application in anti-cancer therapies.") is appealing as a therapeutic vulnerability in precision oncology, as cancer cells that are deficient for one paralogue are selectively sensitive to the inhibition of the second one. Exploitation of this vulnerability would entail the identification of selective inhibitors of VPS4A or VPS4B. In the realms of inflammation and neurodegeneration, it is probably generally desirable to increase ESCRT activity. This might be accomplished by VPS4 enzyme activators or by molecular glues designed to promote the recruitment or assembly of ESCRT complexes at specific sites.

Traditionally, the strongest candidate therapeutic targets are those for which there is human genetic evidence and that belong to classically druggable target classes such as receptors and enzymes. VPS4A/B is an enzyme and manifests synthetic lethality in cancer, thereby qualifying by this criterion. Human genetics connects the loss of function of various CHMP proteins to disease. As non-enzymes and non-receptors, CHMP proteins, and indeed all of the ESCRT system other than VPS4, are not classic druggable targets. Yet a small-molecule inhibitor of protein–protein interactions has been shown to be capable of targeting ESCRT-III assembly[182](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR182 "Knyazeva, A. et al. A chemical inhibitor of IST1–CHMP1B interaction impairs endosomal recycling and induces noncanonical LC3 lipidation. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 121, e2317680121 (2024)."). Traditional criteria for target selection are likely to be too conservative considering the opportunities presented by the ESCRT system. For neurodegenerative diseases associated with loss of ESCRT function, it is probably more desirable to enhance ESCRT assembly than to block it. This might conceivably involve assembly-promoting molecular glues[183](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR183 "Cowan, A. D. & Ciulli, A. Driving E3 ligase substrate specificity for targeted protein degradation: lessons from nature and the laboratory. Annu. Rev. Biochem. 91, 295–319 (2022).") or degraders[184](/articles/s41586-025-08950-y#ref-CR184 "Krone, M. W. & Crews, C. M. Next steps for targeted protein degradation. Cell Chem. Biol. 32, 219–226 (2024).") that target negative regulatory factors. Although ESCRTs have not previously been extensively therapeutically targeted, the wealth of new information about their roles in disease and the growth in new technologies for drugging non-traditional targets is likely to stimulate increased interest in the near future.
